           </span>
           <span title="'r' in 'rye'">
            r
           </span>
           <span title="/ɔː/: 'au' in 'fraud'">
            ɔː
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
           <span title="'w' in 'wind'">
            w
           </span>
           <span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">
            ɑː
           </span>
           <span title="'f' in 'find'">
            f
           </span>
          </span>
          ,
          <span class="wrap">
          </span>
          -
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">
            ɑː
           </span>
           <span title="'f' in 'find'">
            f
           </span>
          </span>
          ,
          <span class="wrap">
          </span>
          -
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">
            ɑː
           </span>
           <span title="'v' in 'vie'">
            v
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key">
        <i title="English pronunciation respelling">
         <span style="font-size:90%">
          VRAWT
         </span>
         -swahf, -⁠slahf, -⁠slahv
        </i>
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <small>
        Polish:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Polish" title="Help:IPA/Polish">
         [ˈvrɔt͡swaf]
        </a>
       </span>
       <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">
        (
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Pl-Wroc%C5%82aw-2.ogg" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/65/Pl-Wroc%C5%82aw-2.ogg" title="Pl-Wrocław-2.ogg">
           listen
          </a>
         </span>
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German
       </a>
       :
       <i lang="de">
        Breslau
       </i>
       <small>
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">
         [ˈbʁɛslaʊ]
        </a>
       </span>
       <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">
        (
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;">
           <a href="/wiki/File:De-Breslau.ogg" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4b/De-Breslau.ogg" title="De-Breslau.ogg">
           listen
          </a>
         </span>
        </span>
        )
       </span>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">
        Czech
       </a>
       :
       <i lang="cs">
        Vratislav
       </i>
       )
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [a]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is a city in southwestern
       <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">
        Poland
       </a>
       and the largest city in the historical region of
       <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">
        Silesia
       </a>
       . It lies on the banks of the River
       <a href="/wiki/Oder" title="Oder">
        Oder
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Silesian_Lowlands" title="Silesian Lowlands">
        Silesian Lowlands
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">
        Central Europe
       </a>
       , roughly 350 kilometres (220 mi) from the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">
        Baltic Sea
       </a>
       to the north and 40 kilometres (25 mi) from the
       <a href="/wiki/Sudetes" title="Sudetes">
        Sudeten Mountains
       </a>
       to the south. The official population of Wrocław in 2020 was 643,782, with a further 1.25 million residing in the
       <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw_metropolitan_area" title="Wrocław metropolitan area">
        metropolitan area
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Wrocław is the historical capital of
       <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">
        Silesia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Silesia" title="Lower Silesia">
        Lower Silesia
       </a>
       . Today, it is the capital of the
       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Silesian_Voivodeship" title="Lower Silesian Voivodeship">
        Lower Silesian Voivodeship
       </a>
       . The history of the city dates back over a thousand years;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       at various times, it has been part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland" title="Kingdom of Poland">
        Kingdom of Poland
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bohemia" title="Kingdom of Bohemia">
        Kingdom of Bohemia
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">
        Kingdom of Hungary
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">
        Habsburg Monarchy
       </a>
       of Austria, the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">
        Kingdom of Prussia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
        Germany
       </a>
       . Wrocław became part of Poland again in 1945 as part of the so-called
       <a href="/wiki/Recovered_Territories" title="Recovered Territories">
        Recovered Territories
       </a>
       , the result of extensive
       <a href="/wiki/Territorial_changes_of_Poland_immediately_after_World_War_II" title="Territorial changes of Poland immediately after World War II">
        border changes and expulsions after the Second World War
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Wrocław is a university city with a student population of over 130,000, making it arguably one of the most youth-oriented cities in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since the beginning of the 20th century, the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="University of Wrocław">
        University of Wrocław
       </a>
       , previously Breslau University, has produced 9
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_laureate" title="Nobel Prize laureate">
        Nobel Prize laureates
       </a>
       and is renowned for its high quality of teaching.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Wrocław also possesses numerous historical landmarks, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Market_Square,_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Market Square, Wrocław">
        Main Market Square
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ostr%C3%B3w_Tumski,_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Ostrów Tumski, Wrocław">
        Cathedral Island
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hala_Stulecia_(Wroc%C5%82aw)" title="Hala Stulecia (Wrocław)">
        Centennial Hall
       </a>
       , which is listed as a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">
        UNESCO World Heritage Site
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1989, 1995 and 2019 Wrocław hosted the European Youth Meetings of the
       <a href="/wiki/Taiz%C3%A9_Community" title="Taizé Community">
        Taizé Community
       </a>
       and hosted the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eucharistic_Congress" title="Eucharistic Congress">
        Eucharistic Congress
       </a>
       in 1997 and the
       <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">
        2012 European Football Championship
       </a>
       . In 2016, the city was a
       <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">
        European Capital of Culture
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Book_Capital" title="World Book Capital">
        World Book Capital
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Also in that year, Wrocław hosted the
       <a href="/wiki/Theatre_Olympics" title="Theatre Olympics">
        Theatre Olympics
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/World_Team_Olympiad" title="World Team Olympiad">
        World Bridge Games
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Film_Awards" title="European Film Awards">
        European Film Awards
       </a>
       . In 2017, the city was host to the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Library_Associations_and_Institutions" title="International Federation of Library Associations and Institutions">
        IFLA
       </a>
       Annual Conference and the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Games" title="World Games">
        World Games
       </a>
       . In 2019, it was named a
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/City_of_Literature" title="City of Literature">
        City of Literature
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Wrocław is classified as a
       <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">
        Gamma global city
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Globalization_and_World_Cities_Research_Network" title="Globalization and World Cities Research Network">
        GaWC
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was placed among the top 100 cities in the world for the Mercer Quality of Living Survey 2015, 2016, 2017, 2019 and in the top 100 of the
       <a href="/wiki/Smart_city" title="Smart city">
        smartest cities
       </a>
       in the world in the IESE Cities in Motion Index 2017 and 2019 report.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In February 2021, belonging to
       <a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">
        Financial Times
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/FDi_Magazine" title="FDi Magazine">
        fDi Magazine
       </a>
       published the report "Global Cities of the Future 2021/2022", in which Wrocław was classified in 1st place among all medium and small cities in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation">

           See also
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41">
         <a href="#Notes">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           14
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           Notes
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42">
         <a href="#References">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           15
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           References
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43">
         <a href="#Bibliography">

          </span>

          </span>

        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44">

          </span>

          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
        Etymology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lauf_Wappen_Civitas_Wratislaviensis.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3069" data-file-width="2571" decoding="async" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Lauf_Wappen_Civitas_Wratislaviensis.jpg/170px-Lauf_Wappen_Civitas_Wratislaviensis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Lauf_Wappen_Civitas_Wratislaviensis.jpg/255px-Lauf_Wappen_Civitas_Wratislaviensis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Lauf_Wappen_Civitas_Wratislaviensis.jpg/340px-Lauf_Wappen_Civitas_Wratislaviensis.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lauf_Wappen_Civitas_Wratislaviensis.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Coat of arms of Wrocław">
          Coat of arms of Wrocław
         </a>
         (with the inscription
         <i>
          Civitas Wratislaviensis
         </i>
         ) in
         <a href="/wiki/Lauf_Castle" title="Lauf Castle">
          Lauf Castle
         </a>
         , c. 1360.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The city is believed to be named after Duke
       <a href="/wiki/Vratislaus_I,_Duke_of_Bohemia" title="Vratislaus I, Duke of Bohemia">
        Vratislav I of Bohemia
       </a>
       from the
       <a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">
        Czech
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/P%C5%99emyslid_dynasty" title="Přemyslid dynasty">
        Přemyslid dynasty
       </a>
       , who ruled the region between 915 and 921.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inyourpocket.com_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-inyourpocket.com-19">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city's name first appeared in the 10th century probably as
       <i>
        Vratislava
       </i>
       . The oldest surviving document containing the recorded name of the city is the chronicle of
       <a href="/wiki/Thietmar_of_Merseburg" title="Thietmar of Merseburg">
        Thietmar of Merseburg
       </a>
       from the early 11th century, which records the city's name as "Wrotizlava", and cites it as a seat of a new
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Wrocław">
        bishopric
       </a>
       at the
       <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Gniezno" title="Congress of Gniezno">
        Congress of Gniezno
       </a>
       . The city's first municipal seal was inscribed with
       <i>
        Sigillum civitatis Wratislavie
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The original
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">
        Old Czech
       </a>
       language version of the name was used in
       <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
        Latin
       </a>
       documents, as
       <i>
        Vratislavia
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Wratislavia
       </i>
       . In the
       <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">
        Polish language
       </a>
       , the city's name
       <i>
        Wrocław
       </i>
       derives from the name
       <a class="extiw" href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wrocis%C5%82aw" title="pl:Wrocisław">
        Wrocisław
       </a>
       , which is the Polish equivalent of the Czech name Vratislav. The earliest variations of this name in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Polish_language" title="Old Polish language">
        Old Polish language
       </a>
       use the letter /l/ instead of /ł/. By the 15th century, the
       <a href="/wiki/Early_New_High_German" title="Early New High German">
        Early New High German
       </a>
       variations of the name,
       <i>
        Breslau
       </i>
       , first began to be used. Despite the noticeable differences in spelling, the numerous German forms were still based on the original
       <a href="/wiki/West_Slavic_languages" title="West Slavic languages">
        West Slavic
       </a>
       name of the city, with the
       <i>
        -Vr-
       </i>
       sound being replaced over time by
       <i>
        -Br-
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the suffix
       <i>
        -slav-
       </i>
       replaced with
       <i>
        -slau-
       </i>
       . These variations included
       <i>
        Vratizlau
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Wratislau
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Wrezlau
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Breßlau
       </i>
       among others.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In other languages, the city's name is: modern
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">
        Czech
       </a>
       :
       <i lang="cs">
        Vratislav
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">
        Hungarian
       </a>
       :
       <i lang="hu">
        Boroszló
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">
        Hebrew
       </a>
       :
       <span dir="rtl" lang="he">
        ורוצלב
       </span>
       ‎ (
       <i>
        Vrotsláv
       </i>
       ),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yiddish_language" title="Yiddish language">
        Yiddish
       </a>
       :
       <span dir="rtl" lang="yi">
        ברעסלוי
       </span>
       ‎ (
       <i>
        Bresloi
       </i>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Silesian_language" title="Silesian language">
        Silesian
       </a>
       :
       <i lang="szl">
        Wrocław
       </i>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lower_Silesian_language" title="Lower Silesian language">
        Lower Silesian
       </a>
       :
       <i lang="sli">
        Brassel
       </i>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">
        Latin
       </a>
       :
       <i lang="la">
        Vratislavia
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Wratislavia
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Budorgis
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Orbis_latinus_oder_Verzeichniss_der_lateinischen_Benennungen_der_bekanntesten_Städte_etc.,_Meere,_Seen,_Berge_und_Flüsse_in_allen_Theilen_der_Erde_nebst_einem_deutsch-lateinischen_Register_derselben._23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Orbis_latinus_oder_Verzeichniss_der_lateinischen_Benennungen_der_bekanntesten_Städte_etc.,_Meere,_Seen,_Berge_und_Flüsse_in_allen_Theilen_der_Erde_nebst_einem_deutsch-lateinischen_Register_derselben.-23">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       People born or resident in the city are known as "
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="List of people from Wrocław">
        Vratislavians
       </a>
       " (
       <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">
        Polish
       </a>
       :
       <i lang="pl">
        wrocławianie
       </i>
       ). During the German era, the demonym was "
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Breslau" title="List of people from Breslau">
        Breslauer
       </a>
       ".
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="History of Wrocław">
        History of Wrocław
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Timeline of Wrocław">
        Timeline of Wrocław
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_history" title="Ancient history">
        ancient
       </a>
       times, there was a place called Budorigum at or near the site of Wrocław. It was already mapped on
       <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">
        Claudius Ptolemy
       </a>
       's map of AD 142–147.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Settlements in the area existed from the 6th century onward during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Migration_period" title="Migration period">
        migration period
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C5%9Al%C4%99%C5%BCanie" title="Ślężanie">
        Ślężans
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/West_Slavs" title="West Slavs">
        West Slavic
       </a>
       tribe, settled on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oder_river" title="Oder river">
        Oder river
       </a>
       and erected a fortified
       <a href="/wiki/Gord_(archaeology)" title="Gord (archaeology)">
        gord
       </a>
       on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ostr%C3%B3w_Tumski_in_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Ostrów Tumski in Wrocław">
        Ostrów Tumski
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Wrocław originated at the intersection of two
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_route" title="Trade route">
        trade routes
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Via_Regia" title="Via Regia">
        Via Regia
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Amber_Road" title="Amber Road">
        Amber Road
       </a>
       . The city was first recognized in the 10th century as
       <i>
        Vratislavia
       </i>
       on account of the Bohemian duke
       <a href="/wiki/Vratislaus_I,_Duke_of_Bohemia" title="Vratislaus I, Duke of Bohemia">
        Vratislav I
       </a>
       's stronghold there, hence the name.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inyourpocket.com_19-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-inyourpocket.com-19">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       When in 985, Duke
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mieszko_I_of_Poland" title="Mieszko I of Poland">
        Mieszko I of Poland
       </a>
       conquered Silesia, Vratislavia's
       <a href="/wiki/Polonization" title="Polonization">
        polonised
       </a>
       form over time became
       <i>
        Wrocław
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The town was mentioned explicitly in the year
       <a href="/wiki/AD_1000" title="AD 1000">
        1000 AD
       </a>
       in connection with its promotion to an
       <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_see" title="Episcopal see">
        episcopal see
       </a>
       during the
       <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Gniezno" title="Congress of Gniezno">
        Congress of Gniezno
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
       .mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}
      </style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ko%C5%9Bci%C3%B3%C5%82_%C5%9Bw._Idziego_i_brama_Kluskowa_-_plac_Katedralny_l_fot_BMaliszewska.jpg">
            <img alt="Church of Saint Giles" data-file-height="669" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Ko%C5%9Bci%C3%B3%C5%82_%C5%9Bw._Idziego_i_brama_Kluskowa_-_plac_Katedralny_l_fot_BMaliszewska.jpg/220px-Ko%C5%9Bci%C3%B3%C5%82_%C5%9Bw._Idziego_i_brama_Kluskowa_-_plac_Katedralny_l_fot_BMaliszewska.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Ko%C5%9Bci%C3%B3%C5%82_%C5%9Bw._Idziego_i_brama_Kluskowa_-_plac_Katedralny_l_fot_BMaliszewska.jpg/330px-Ko%C5%9Bci%C3%B3%C5%82_%C5%9Bw._Idziego_i_brama_Kluskowa_-_plac_Katedralny_l_fot_BMaliszewska.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Ko%C5%9Bci%C3%B3%C5%82_%C5%9Bw._Idziego_i_brama_Kluskowa_-_plac_Katedralny_l_fot_BMaliszewska.jpg/440px-Ko%C5%9Bci%C3%B3%C5%82_%C5%9Bw._Idziego_i_brama_Kluskowa_-_plac_Katedralny_l_fot_BMaliszewska.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PL-DS,_Wroc%C5%82aw,_pl._Katedralny_18;_Plebania;_58.jpg">
            <img alt="Church of Saint Giles seen from above" data-file-height="3318" data-file-width="4977" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/PL-DS%2C_Wroc%C5%82aw%2C_pl._Katedralny_18%3B_Plebania%3B_58.jpg/220px-PL-DS%2C_Wroc%C5%82aw%2C_pl._Katedralny_18%3B_Plebania%3B_58.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/PL-DS%2C_Wroc%C5%82aw%2C_pl._Katedralny_18%3B_Plebania%3B_58.jpg/330px-PL-DS%2C_Wroc%C5%82aw%2C_pl._Katedralny_18%3B_Plebania%3B_58.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/PL-DS%2C_Wroc%C5%82aw%2C_pl._Katedralny_18%3B_Plebania%3B_58.jpg/440px-PL-DS%2C_Wroc%C5%82aw%2C_pl._Katedralny_18%3B_Plebania%3B_58.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a class="extiw" href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ko%C5%9Bci%C3%B3%C5%82_%C5%9Bw._Idziego_we_Wroc%C5%82awiu" title="pl:Kościół św. Idziego we Wrocławiu">
            Church of Saint Giles (pl)
           </a>
           erected in the 1220s at
           <a href="/wiki/Ostr%C3%B3w_Tumski,_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Ostrów Tumski, Wrocław">
            Ostrów Tumski
           </a>
           , the oldest section of Wrocław
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During Wrocław's early history, control over it changed hands between the
       <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Bohemia" title="Duchy of Bohemia">
        Duchy of Bohemia
       </a>
       (until 992, then 1038–1054), the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Poland_(966%E2%80%931025)" title="Duchy of Poland (966–1025)">
        Duchy of Poland
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland_(1025%E2%80%931385)" title="Kingdom of Poland (1025–1385)">
        Kingdom of Poland
       </a>
       (992–1038 and 1054–1202). Following the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Poland_(966%E2%80%931385)" title="History of Poland (966–1385)">
        fragmentation of the Kingdom of Poland
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Piast_dynasty" title="Piast dynasty">
        Piast dynasty
       </a>
       ruled the
       <a href="/wiki/Duchies_of_Silesia" title="Duchies of Silesia">
        Duchy of Silesia
       </a>
       . One of the most important events during this period was the foundation of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Diocese of Wrocław">
        Diocese of Wrocław
       </a>
       by the Polish Duke and from 1025, King
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boles%C5%82aw_the_Brave" title="Bolesław the Brave">
        Bolesław the Brave
       </a>
       in 1000. Along with the
       <a href="/wiki/Diocese" title="Diocese">
        Bishoprics
       </a>
       of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Krak%C3%B3w" title="Bishopric of Kraków">
        Kraków
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Ko%C5%82obrzeg" title="Bishopric of Kołobrzeg">
        Kołobrzeg
       </a>
       , Wrocław was placed under the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Gniezno" title="Archbishopric of Gniezno">
        Archbishopric of Gniezno
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Poland" title="Greater Poland">
        Greater Poland
       </a>
       , founded by
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_Sylvester_II" title="Pope Sylvester II">
        Pope Sylvester II
       </a>
       through the intercession of Polish Duke
       <a href="/wiki/Boles%C5%82aw_I_the_Brave" title="Bolesław I the Brave">
        Bolesław I the Brave
       </a>
       and Emperor
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otto_III" title="Otto III">
        Otto III
       </a>
       in 1000, during the Gniezno Congress.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the years 1034–1038 the city was affected by
       <a href="/wiki/Pagan_reaction_in_Poland" title="Pagan reaction in Poland">
        Pagan reaction in Poland
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mikrokosmos_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mikrokosmos-29">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The city became a commercial centre and expanded to
       <a href="/wiki/Wyspa_Piasek" title="Wyspa Piasek">
        Wyspa Piasek
       </a>
       (Sand Island), and then onto the left bank of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_Oder" title="River Oder">
        River Oder
       </a>
       . Around 1000, the town had about 1,000 inhabitants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weczerka_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-weczerka-30">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1109 during the
       <a class="extiw" href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wojna_polsko-niemiecka_1109" title="pl:Wojna polsko-niemiecka 1109">
        Polish-German war
       </a>
       , Prince
       <a href="/wiki/Boles%C5%82aw_III_Wrymouth" title="Bolesław III Wrymouth">
        Bolesław III Wrymouth
       </a>
       defeated the King of Germany
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Henry V, Holy Roman Emperor">
        Henry V
       </a>
       at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hundsfeld" title="Battle of Hundsfeld">
        Battle of Hundsfeld
       </a>
       , stopping the German advance into Poland. The medieval chronicle,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Gesta_principum_Polonorum" title="Gesta principum Polonorum">
         Gesta principum Polonorum
        </a>
       </i>
       (1112–1116) by
       <a href="/wiki/Gallus_Anonymus" title="Gallus Anonymus">
        Gallus Anonymus
       </a>
       , named Wrocław, along with
       <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">
        Kraków
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sandomierz" title="Sandomierz">
        Sandomierz
       </a>
       , as one of three capitals of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland_(1025%E2%80%931385)" title="Kingdom of Poland (1025–1385)">
        Polish Kingdom
       </a>
       . Also, the
       <a href="/wiki/Tabula_Rogeriana" title="Tabula Rogeriana">
        Tabula Rogeriana
       </a>
       a book written by the Arab geographer Muhammad al-Idrisi in 1154, describes Wrocław as one of the Polish cities, alongside Kraków,
       <a href="/wiki/Gniezno" title="Gniezno">
        Gniezno
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sieradz" title="Sieradz">
        Sieradz
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/%C5%81%C4%99czyca" title="Łęczyca">
        Łęczyca
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Santok" title="Santok">
        Santok
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Modlitwy_drukowane_po_polsku_w_r._1475.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="796" data-file-width="463" decoding="async" height="275" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Modlitwy_drukowane_po_polsku_w_r._1475.JPG/160px-Modlitwy_drukowane_po_polsku_w_r._1475.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Modlitwy_drukowane_po_polsku_w_r._1475.JPG/240px-Modlitwy_drukowane_po_polsku_w_r._1475.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Modlitwy_drukowane_po_polsku_w_r._1475.JPG/320px-Modlitwy_drukowane_po_polsku_w_r._1475.JPG 2x" width="160"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Modlitwy_drukowane_po_polsku_w_r._1475.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The oldest printed text in the
         <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">
          Polish language
         </a>
         –
         <i>
          Statuta Synodalia Episcoporum Wratislaviensis
         </i>
         , printed in Wrocław by Kasper Elyan, 1475
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       By 1139, a settlement belonging to Governor
       <a href="/wiki/Piotr_W%C5%82ostowic" title="Piotr Włostowic">
        Piotr Włostowic
       </a>
       (also known as Piotr Włast
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dunin_(surname)" title="Dunin (surname)">
        Dunin
       </a>
       ) was built, and another on the left bank of the River Oder, near the present site of the university. While the city was largely Polish, it also had communities of Bohemians (
       <a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">
        Czechs
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
        Germans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Walloons" title="Walloons">
        Walloons
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">
        Jews
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weczerka1_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-weczerka1-32">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mikrokosmos_29-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mikrokosmos-29">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kulak_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kulak-33">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 13th century, Wrocław was the political centre of the divided
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland_(1025%E2%80%931385)" title="Kingdom of Poland (1025–1385)">
        Polish kingdom
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Henryk_Brodaty_i_jego_czasy_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Henryk_Brodaty_i_jego_czasy-34">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In April 1241, during the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Mongol_invasion_of_Poland" title="First Mongol invasion of Poland">
        First Mongol invasion of Poland
       </a>
       , the city was abandoned by its inhabitants and burnt down for strategic reasons. During the battles with the Mongols
       <a class="extiw" href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zamek_na_Ostrowie_Tumskim_we_Wroc%C5%82awiu" title="pl:Zamek na Ostrowie Tumskim we Wrocławiu">
        Wrocław Castle
       </a>
       was successfully defended by
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_the_Pious" title="Henry II the Pious">
        Henry II the Pious
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mikrokosmos2_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mikrokosmos2-35">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After the Mongol invasion the town was partly populated by
       <a href="/wiki/Ostsiedlung" title="Ostsiedlung">
        German settlers
       </a>
       who, in the ensuing centuries, gradually became its dominant population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thum,_p._316_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Thum,_p._316-36">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city, however, retained its multi-ethnic character, a reflection of its importance as a trading post on the junction of the Via Regia and the Amber Road.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mikrokosmos3_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mikrokosmos3-37">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       With the influx of settlers, the town expanded and in 1242 came under
       <a href="/wiki/German_town_law" title="German town law">
        German town law
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/City_council" title="City council">
        city council
       </a>
       used both
       <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
        Latin
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German
       </a>
       , and the early forms of the name "Breslau", the German name of the city, appeared for the first time in its written records.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thum,_p._316_36-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Thum,_p._316-36">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Polish gradually ceased to be used in the town books, while it survived in the courts until 1337.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kulak_33-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kulak-33">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The enlarged town covered around 60 hectares (150 acres), and the new
       <a href="/wiki/Market_Square,_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Market Square, Wrocław">
        main market square
       </a>
       , surrounded by timber-frame houses, became the trade centre of the town. The original foundation,
       <a href="/wiki/Ostr%C3%B3w_Tumski,_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Ostrów Tumski, Wrocław">
        Ostrów Tumski
       </a>
       , became its religious centre. The city gained
       <a href="/wiki/Magdeburg_rights" title="Magdeburg rights">
        Magdeburg rights
       </a>
       in 1261. While the Polish Piast dynasty remained in control of the region, the ability of the city council to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Self-Government" title="Self-Government">
        govern
       </a>
       itself independently increased.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-google-38">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1274 prince
       <a href="/wiki/Henryk_IV_Probus" title="Henryk IV Probus">
        Henryk IV Probus
       </a>
       gave the city its
       <a href="/wiki/Staple_right" title="Staple right">
        staple right
       </a>
       . In the 13th century, two Polish monarchs were buried in Wrocław churches founded by them,
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_the_Pious" title="Henry II the Pious">
        Henry II the Pious
       </a>
       in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_St._Vincent_and_St._James,_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Cathedral of St. Vincent and St. James, Wrocław">
        St. Vincent church
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gosc_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-gosc-39">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and Henryk IV Probus in the Holy Cross church.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Breslau,_Martinskirche_von_Norden,_3.jpeg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2688" data-file-width="2688" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Breslau%2C_Martinskirche_von_Norden%2C_3.jpeg/220px-Breslau%2C_Martinskirche_von_Norden%2C_3.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Breslau%2C_Martinskirche_von_Norden%2C_3.jpeg/330px-Breslau%2C_Martinskirche_von_Norden%2C_3.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Breslau%2C_Martinskirche_von_Norden%2C_3.jpeg/440px-Breslau%2C_Martinskirche_von_Norden%2C_3.jpeg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Breslau,_Martinskirche_von_Norden,_3.jpeg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zamek_na_Ostrowie_Tumskim_we_Wroc%C5%82awiu" title="pl:Zamek na Ostrowie Tumskim we Wrocławiu">
          St Martin's Church
         </a>
         , the only remaining part of the medieval
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piast" title="Piast">
          Piast
         </a>
         stronghold that once stood in Wrocław
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Wrocław, which for 350 years had been mostly under Polish
       <a href="/wiki/Hegemony" title="Hegemony">
        hegemony
       </a>
       , fell in 1335, after the death of
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_VI_the_Good" title="Henry VI the Good">
        Henry VI the Good
       </a>
       , to the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bohemia" title="Kingdom of Bohemia">
        Kingdom of Bohemia
       </a>
       , then a part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">
        Holy Roman Empire
       </a>
       . Between 1342 and 1344, two fires destroyed large parts of the city. In 1387 the city joined the
       <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">
        Hanseatic League
       </a>
       . On 5 June 1443, the city was rocked by an earthquake, estimated at ca. 6 on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richter_scale" title="Richter scale">
        Richter scale
       </a>
       , which destroyed or seriously damaged many of its buildings.
      </p>
      <p>
       Between 1469 and 1490, Wrocław was part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">
        Kingdom of Hungary
       </a>
       , and king
       <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Corvinus" title="Matthias Corvinus">
        Matthias Corvinus
       </a>
       was said to have had a Vratislavian mistress who bore him a son.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1474, after almost a century, the city left the Hanseatic League. Also in 1474, the city was besieged by combined Polish-Czech forces. However, in November 1474, Kings
       <a href="/wiki/Casimir_IV_Jagiellon" title="Casimir IV Jagiellon">
        Casimir IV of Poland
       </a>
       , his son
       <a href="/wiki/Vladislaus_II_of_Hungary" title="Vladislaus II of Hungary">
        Vladislaus II of Bohemia
       </a>
       , and Matthias Corvinus of Hungary met in the nearby village of Muchobór Wielki (present-day a district of Wrocław), and in December 1474 a
       <a href="/wiki/Ceasefire" title="Ceasefire">
        ceasefire
       </a>
       was signed according to which the city remained under Hungarian rule.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The following year was marked by the publication in Wrocław of the
       <i>
        Statuta Synodalia Episcoporum Wratislaviensium
       </i>
       (1475) by Kasper Elyan, the first ever
       <a href="/wiki/Incunable" title="Incunable">
        Incunable
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">
        Polish
       </a>
       , containing the proceedings and prayers of the Wrocław bishops.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Renaissance_and_the_Reformation">
        Renaissance and the Reformation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Renaissance and the Reformation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Breslau1562Weihner.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="8963" data-file-width="9000" decoding="async" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Breslau1562Weihner.jpg/220px-Breslau1562Weihner.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Breslau1562Weihner.jpg/330px-Breslau1562Weihner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Breslau1562Weihner.jpg/440px-Breslau1562Weihner.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Breslau1562Weihner.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of the city from 1562, with its fortifications on the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oder_River" title="Oder River">
          Oder River
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the 16th century, the Breslauer Schöps
       <a href="/wiki/Beer_style" title="Beer style">
        beer style
       </a>
       was created in Wrocław.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">
        Protestant Reformation
       </a>
       reached the city in 1518 and it converted to the new rite. However, starting in 1526
       <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">
        Silesia
       </a>
       was ruled by the Catholic
       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">
        House of Habsburg
       </a>
       . In 1618, it supported the
       <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Revolt" title="Bohemian Revolt">
        Bohemian Revolt
       </a>
       out of fear of losing the right to
       <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">
        religious freedom
       </a>
       . During the ensuing
       <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">
        Thirty Years' War
       </a>
       , the city was occupied by
       <a href="/wiki/Saxony" title="Saxony">
        Saxon
       </a>
       and Swedish troops and lost thousands of inhabitants to the
       <a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">
        plague
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">
        Emperor
       </a>
       brought in the
       <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">
        Counter-Reformation
       </a>
       by encouraging Catholic orders to settle in the city, starting in 1610 with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franciscan" title="Franciscan">
        Franciscans
       </a>
       , followed by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit">
        Jesuits
       </a>
       , then
       <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Friars_Minor_Capuchin" title="Order of Friars Minor Capuchin">
        Capuchins
       </a>
       , and finally
       <a href="/wiki/Ursulines" title="Ursulines">
        Ursuline nuns
       </a>
       in 1687.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inyourpocket.com_19-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-inyourpocket.com-19">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These orders erected buildings that shaped the city's appearance until 1945. At the end of the Thirty Years' War, however, it was one of only a few Silesian cities to stay Protestant.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Polish Municipal school opened in 1666 and lasted until 1766. Precise record-keeping of births and deaths by the city fathers led to the use of their data for analysis of mortality, first by
       <a href="/wiki/John_Graunt" title="John Graunt">
        John Graunt
       </a>
       and then, based on data provided to him by Breslau professor
       <a href="/wiki/Caspar_Neumann" title="Caspar Neumann">
        Caspar Neumann
       </a>
       , by
       <a href="/wiki/Edmond_Halley" title="Edmond Halley">
        Edmond Halley
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Halley's tables and analysis, published in 1693, are considered to be the first true actuarial tables, and thus the foundation of modern
       <a href="/wiki/Actuarial_science" title="Actuarial science">
        actuarial science
       </a>
       . During the Counter-Reformation, the intellectual life of the city flourished, as the Protestant
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bourgeois" title="Bourgeois">
        bourgeoisie
       </a>
       lost some of its dominance to the Catholic orders as patrons of the arts.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Enlightenment_period">
        Enlightenment period
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Enlightenment period">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stammbuch_Johann_Gottfried_R%C3%BCde_Illustration_Breslau_1760.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="541" data-file-width="930" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Stammbuch_Johann_Gottfried_R%C3%BCde_Illustration_Breslau_1760.jpg/220px-Stammbuch_Johann_Gottfried_R%C3%BCde_Illustration_Breslau_1760.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Stammbuch_Johann_Gottfried_R%C3%BCde_Illustration_Breslau_1760.jpg/330px-Stammbuch_Johann_Gottfried_R%C3%BCde_Illustration_Breslau_1760.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Stammbuch_Johann_Gottfried_R%C3%BCde_Illustration_Breslau_1760.jpg/440px-Stammbuch_Johann_Gottfried_R%C3%BCde_Illustration_Breslau_1760.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stammbuch_Johann_Gottfried_R%C3%BCde_Illustration_Breslau_1760.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Breslau_(1757)" title="Battle of Breslau (1757)">
          Battle of Breslau
         </a>
         during the
         <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">
          Seven Years' War
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/Third_Silesian_War" title="Third Silesian War">
          Third Silesian War
         </a>
         1756–1763)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The city became the centre of German
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baroque_literature" title="Baroque literature">
        Baroque literature
       </a>
       and was home to the First and Second Silesian school of poets.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the 1740s the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">
        Kingdom of Prussia
       </a>
       annexed the city and most of Silesia during the
       <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">
        War of the Austrian Succession
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">
        Habsburg
       </a>
       Empress
       <a href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa" title="Maria Theresa">
        Maria Theresa
       </a>
       ceded most of the territory in the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Breslau" title="Treaty of Breslau">
        Treaty of Breslau
       </a>
       in 1742 to
       <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">
        Prussia
       </a>
       . Austria attempted to recover Silesia during the
       <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">
        Seven Years' War
       </a>
       at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Breslau_(1757)" title="Battle of Breslau (1757)">
        Battle of Breslau
       </a>
       , but they were unsuccessful. The Venetian Italian adventurer,
       <a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Casanova" title="Giacomo Casanova">
        Giacomo Casanova
       </a>
       , stayed in Breslau in 1766.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Napoleonic_Wars">
        Napoleonic Wars
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Napoleonic Wars">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Entr%C3%A9e_du_Prince_J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_%C3%A0_Breslau_le_7_janvier_1807.PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="459" data-file-width="731" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Entr%C3%A9e_du_Prince_J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_%C3%A0_Breslau_le_7_janvier_1807.PNG/220px-Entr%C3%A9e_du_Prince_J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_%C3%A0_Breslau_le_7_janvier_1807.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Entr%C3%A9e_du_Prince_J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_%C3%A0_Breslau_le_7_janvier_1807.PNG/330px-Entr%C3%A9e_du_Prince_J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_%C3%A0_Breslau_le_7_janvier_1807.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Entr%C3%A9e_du_Prince_J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_%C3%A0_Breslau_le_7_janvier_1807.PNG/440px-Entr%C3%A9e_du_Prince_J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_%C3%A0_Breslau_le_7_janvier_1807.PNG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Entr%C3%A9e_du_Prince_J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_%C3%A0_Breslau_le_7_janvier_1807.PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Entry of Prince
         <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_Bonaparte" title="Jérôme Bonaparte">
          Jérôme Bonaparte
         </a>
         into Breslau, 7 January 1807
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the
       <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">
        Napoleonic Wars
       </a>
       , it was occupied by the
       <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_the_Rhine" title="Confederation of the Rhine">
        Confederation of the Rhine
       </a>
       army. The fortifications of the city were levelled, and monasteries and cloisters were seized.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inyourpocket.com_19-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-inyourpocket.com-19">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Protestant
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viadrina_European_University" title="Viadrina European University">
        Viadrina European University
       </a>
       at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_am_Oder" title="Frankfurt am Oder">
        Frankfurt am Oder
       </a>
       was relocated to Breslau in 1811, and united with the local Jesuit University to create the new Silesian Frederick-William University (
       <i>
        Schlesische Friedrich-Wilhelm-Universität
       </i>
       , now the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="University of Wrocław">
        University of Wrocław
       </a>
       ). The city became a centre of the German Liberation movement against Napoleon, and a gathering place for volunteers from all over Germany. The city was the centre of
       <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">
        Prussian
       </a>
       mobilisation for the campaign which ended at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leipzig" title="Battle of Leipzig">
        Battle of Leipzig
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_age">
        Industrial age
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Industrial age">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_the_Rhine" title="Confederation of the Rhine">
        Confederation of the Rhine
       </a>
       had increased prosperity in Silesia and in the city. The removal of fortifications opened room for the city to expand beyond its former limits. Breslau became an important railway hub and industrial centre, notably for linen and
       <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">
        cotton
       </a>
       manufacture and the metal industry. The reconstructed university served as a major centre of science;
       <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Brahms" title="Johannes Brahms">
        Johannes Brahms
       </a>
       later wrote his
       <a href="/wiki/Academic_Festival_Overture" title="Academic Festival Overture">
        Academic Festival Overture
       </a>
       to thank the university for an honorary doctorate awarded in 1879.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1821, the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Wrocław">
        (Arch)Diocese of Breslau
       </a>
       withdrew from dependence on the Polish archbishopric of Gniezno, and Breslau became an exempt see. On 10 October 1854, the
       <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Theological_Seminary_of_Breslau" title="Jewish Theological Seminary of Breslau">
        Jewish Theological Seminary
       </a>
       opened. The institution was the first modern rabbinical seminary in Central Europe. In 1863 the brothers Karl and Louis Stangen founded the travel agency Stangen, the second travel agency in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wroc%C5%82aw_-_Pa%C5%82ac_Kr%C3%B3lewski.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Wroc%C5%82aw_-_Pa%C5%82ac_Kr%C3%B3lewski.jpg/220px-Wroc%C5%82aw_-_Pa%C5%82ac_Kr%C3%B3lewski.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Wroc%C5%82aw_-_Pa%C5%82ac_Kr%C3%B3lewski.jpg/330px-Wroc%C5%82aw_-_Pa%C5%82ac_Kr%C3%B3lewski.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Wroc%C5%82aw_-_Pa%C5%82ac_Kr%C3%B3lewski.jpg/440px-Wroc%C5%82aw_-_Pa%C5%82ac_Kr%C3%B3lewski.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wroc%C5%82aw_-_Pa%C5%82ac_Kr%C3%B3lewski.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Royal_Palace,_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Royal Palace, Wrocław">
          Royal Palace
         </a>
         from 1717 was once the residence of Prussian monarchs and German emperors. It now houses the City Museum.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The city was an important center of the
       <a href="/wiki/Resistance_movements_in_partitioned_Poland_(1795%E2%80%931918)" title="Resistance movements in partitioned Poland (1795–1918)">
        Polish secret resistance movement
       </a>
       and the seat of a Polish uprising committee before and during the
       <a href="/wiki/January_Uprising" title="January Uprising">
        January Uprising
       </a>
       of 1863–1864 in the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Partition" title="Russian Partition">
        Russian Partition
       </a>
       of Poland.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Local Poles took part in Polish national mourning after the Russian massacre of Polish protesters in
       <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">
        Warsaw
       </a>
       in February 1861, and also organized several patriotic Polish church services throughout 1861.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Secret Polish correspondence, weapons, and insurgents were transported through the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After the outbreak of the uprising in 1863, the Prussian police carried out mass searches of Polish homes, especially those of Poles who had recently come to the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city's inhabitants, both Poles and Germans, excluding the German aristocracy, largely sympathized with the uprising, and some Germans even joined local Poles in their secret activities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In June 1863 the city was officially confirmed as the seat of secret Polish insurgent authorities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In January 1864, the Prussian police arrested a number of members of the Polish insurgent movement.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Breslau_um_1900.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2502" data-file-width="3438" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Breslau_um_1900.jpg/220px-Breslau_um_1900.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Breslau_um_1900.jpg/330px-Breslau_um_1900.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Breslau_um_1900.jpg/440px-Breslau_um_1900.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Breslau_um_1900.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw_Town_Hall" title="Wrocław Town Hall">
          Old Town Hall
         </a>
         , 1900
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Germany" title="Unification of Germany">
        Unification of Germany
       </a>
       in 1871 turned Breslau into the sixth-largest city in the
       <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">
        German Empire
       </a>
       . Its population more than tripled to over half a million between 1860 and 1910. The 1900 census listed 422,709 residents.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1890, construction began of
       <a class="extiw" href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twierdza_Wroc%C5%82aw_1890%E2%80%931918" title="pl:Twierdza Wrocław 1890–1918">
        Breslau Fortress
       </a>
       as the city's defenses. Important landmarks were inaugurated in 1910, the
       <i>
        Kaiser bridge
       </i>
       (today
       <a href="/wiki/Grunwald_Bridge" title="Grunwald Bridge">
        Grunwald Bridge
       </a>
       ) and the
       <i>
        Technical University
       </i>
       , which now houses the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw_University_of_Technology" title="Wrocław University of Technology">
        Wrocław University of Technology
       </a>
       .
The 1900 census listed 98% of the population as German-speakers, with 5,363 Polish-speakers (1.3%), and 3,103 (0.7%) as bilingual in German and Polish.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-konversationslexikon394_60-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-konversationslexikon394-60">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The population was 58% Protestant, 37% Catholic (including at least 2% Polish)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-harasimowicz_61-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-harasimowicz-61">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and 5% Jewish (totaling 20,536 in the 1905 census).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-konversationslexikon394_60-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-konversationslexikon394-60">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_community" title="Jewish community">
        Jewish community
       </a>
       of Breslau was among the most important in Germany, producing several distinguished artists and scientists.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wisc_62-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-wisc-62">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       From 1912, the head of the university's Department of Psychiatry and director of the Clinic of Psychiatry (
       <i>
        Königlich Psychiatrischen und Nervenklinik
       </i>
       ) was
       <a href="/wiki/Alois_Alzheimer" title="Alois Alzheimer">
        Alois Alzheimer
       </a>
       and, that same year, professor
       <a href="/wiki/William_Stern_(psychologist)" title="William Stern (psychologist)">
        William Stern
       </a>
       introduced the concept of
       <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_quotient" title="Intelligence quotient">
        IQ
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Breslau_Ring_Ostseite_(1890-1900).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2511" data-file-width="3439" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Breslau_Ring_Ostseite_%281890-1900%29.jpg/220px-Breslau_Ring_Ostseite_%281890-1900%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Breslau_Ring_Ostseite_%281890-1900%29.jpg/330px-Breslau_Ring_Ostseite_%281890-1900%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Breslau_Ring_Ostseite_%281890-1900%29.jpg/440px-Breslau_Ring_Ostseite_%281890-1900%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Breslau_Ring_Ostseite_(1890-1900).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Market_Square,_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Market Square, Wrocław">
          Market Square
         </a>
         , 1890–1900
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dom_Towarowy_%22Feniks%22_Rynek_31,32.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Dom_Towarowy_%22Feniks%22_Rynek_31%2C32.JPG/220px-Dom_Towarowy_%22Feniks%22_Rynek_31%2C32.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Dom_Towarowy_%22Feniks%22_Rynek_31%2C32.JPG/330px-Dom_Towarowy_%22Feniks%22_Rynek_31%2C32.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Dom_Towarowy_%22Feniks%22_Rynek_31%2C32.JPG/440px-Dom_Towarowy_%22Feniks%22_Rynek_31%2C32.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dom_Towarowy_%22Feniks%22_Rynek_31,32.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Barasch_Brothers%27_Department_Store" title="Barasch Brothers' Department Store">
          Feniks Department Store
         </a>
         , built in 1902–1904
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1913, the newly built
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hala_Stulecia_(Wroc%C5%82aw)" title="Hala Stulecia (Wrocław)">
        Centennial Hall
       </a>
       housed an exhibition commemorating the 100th anniversary of the historical
       <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Sixth_Coalition" title="War of the Sixth Coalition">
        German Wars of Liberation
       </a>
       against
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_I_of_France" title="Napoleon I of France">
        Napoleon
       </a>
       and the first award of the
       <a href="/wiki/Iron_Cross" title="Iron Cross">
        Iron Cross
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Following the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">
        First World War
       </a>
       , Breslau became the capital of the newly created Prussian
       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Lower_Silesia" title="Province of Lower Silesia">
        Province of Lower Silesia
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">
        Weimar Republic
       </a>
       in 1919. After the war the Polish community began holding masses in Polish at the Church of Saint Anne, and, as of 1921, at St. Martin's and a Polish School was founded by Helena Adamczewska.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Microcosm,_page_361_65-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Microcosm,_page_361-65">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1920 a Polish
       <a href="/wiki/Consulate" title="Consulate">
        consulate
       </a>
       was opened on the Main Square.
      </p>
      <p>
       In August 1920, during the Polish
       <a href="/wiki/Silesian_Uprisings" title="Silesian Uprisings">
        Silesian Uprising
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Upper_Silesia" title="Upper Silesia">
        Upper Silesia
       </a>
       , the Polish Consulate and School were destroyed, while the Polish Library was burned down by a mob. The number of Poles as a percentage of the total population fell to just 0.5% after the re-emergence of
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Poland_(1918%E2%80%931939)" title="History of Poland (1918–1939)">
        Poland
       </a>
       as a state in 1918, when many moved to Poland.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-harasimowicz_61-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-harasimowicz-61">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">
        Antisemitic
       </a>
       riots occurred in 1923.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Microcosm_396_66-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Microcosm_396-66">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The city boundaries were expanded between 1925 and 1930 to include an area of 175 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (68 sq mi) with a population of 600,000. In 1929, the
       <a href="/wiki/Deutscher_Werkbund" title="Deutscher Werkbund">
        Werkbund
       </a>
       opened
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/WUWA_(Breslau)" title="WUWA (Breslau)">
         WuWa
        </a>
       </i>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German
       </a>
       :
       <i lang="de">
        Wohnungs- und Werkraumausstellung
       </i>
       ) in Breslau-Scheitnig, an international showcase of
       <a href="/wiki/Modern_architecture" title="Modern architecture">
        modern architecture
       </a>
       by architects of the Silesian branch of the Werkbund. In June 1930, Breslau hosted the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/German_Combat_Games" title="German Combat Games">
         Deutsche Kampfspiele
        </a>
       </i>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Sport" title="Sport">
        sporting
       </a>
       event for German athletes after Germany was excluded from the
       <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">
        Olympic Games
       </a>
       after World War I. The number of Jews remaining in Breslau fell from 23,240 in 1925 to 10,659 in 1933.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Up to the beginning of World War II, Breslau was the largest city in Germany east of
       <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">
        Berlin
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Breslau_NARA-68155041.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2684" data-file-width="3748" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Breslau_NARA-68155041.jpg/220px-Breslau_NARA-68155041.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Breslau_NARA-68155041.jpg/330px-Breslau_NARA-68155041.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Breslau_NARA-68155041.jpg/440px-Breslau_NARA-68155041.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Breslau_NARA-68155041.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Aerial view of pre-war Breslau, 1920
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Known as a stronghold of
       <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">
        left wing liberalism
       </a>
