       during the German Empire, Breslau eventually became one of the strongest support bases of the
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">
        Nazi Party
       </a>
       , which in the 1932 elections received 44% of the city's vote, their third-highest total in all Germany.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mikrokosmos4_70-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mikrokosmos4-70">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KZ_D%C3%BCrrgoy" title="KZ Dürrgoy">
        KZ Dürrgoy
       </a>
       , one of the first concentration camps in the
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
        Third Reich
       </a>
       , was set up in the city in 1933.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ziesak_71-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ziesak-71">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After
       <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">
        Hitler
       </a>
       's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NSDAP#In_power:_1933–1945" title="NSDAP">
        appointment as German Chancellor
       </a>
       in 1933, political enemies of the Nazis were persecuted, and their institutions closed or destroyed. The
       <a href="/wiki/Gestapo" title="Gestapo">
        Gestapo
       </a>
       began actions against Polish and Jewish students (see:
       <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Theological_Seminary_of_Breslau" title="Jewish Theological Seminary of Breslau">
        Jewish Theological Seminary of Breslau
       </a>
       ),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KPD" title="KPD">
        Communists
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">
        Social Democrats
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trade_unionists" title="Trade unionists">
        trade unionists
       </a>
       . Arrests were made for speaking Polish in public, and in 1938 the Nazi-controlled police destroyed the Polish cultural centre.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Microcosm_395_72-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Microcosm_395-72">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kulak_252_73-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kulak_252-73">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In June 1939, Polish students were expelled from the university.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mc_74-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mc-74">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Also many other people seen as "undesirable" by the
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
        Third Reich
       </a>
       were sent to
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">
        concentration camps
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Microcosm_395_72-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Microcosm_395-72">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A network of
       <a href="/wiki/Internment" title="Internment">
        concentration camps
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Arbeitslager" title="Arbeitslager">
        forced labour camps
       </a>
       was established around Breslau to serve industrial concerns, including
       <a href="/wiki/FAMO" title="FAMO">
        FAMO
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Junkers" title="Junkers">
        Junkers
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Krupp" title="Krupp">
        Krupp
       </a>
       . Tens of thousand of forced laborers were imprisoned there.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RM_75-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-RM-75">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The last big event organized by the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_League_of_the_Reich_for_Physical_Exercise" title="National Socialist League of the Reich for Physical Exercise">
        National Socialist League of the Reich for Physical Exercise
       </a>
       , called
       <a href="/wiki/Deutsches_Turn-_und_Sportfest_1938" title="Deutsches Turn- und Sportfest 1938">
        Deutsches Turn-und-Sportfest
       </a>
       (Gym and Sports Festivities), took place in Breslau from 26 to 31 July 1938. The Sportsfest was held to commemorate the 125th anniversary of the German Wars of Liberation against Napoleon's invasion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SF_76-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SF-76">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">
        Second World War
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Second World War">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_of_Wroclaw_1945.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="793" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Cathedral_of_Wroclaw_1945.jpg/220px-Cathedral_of_Wroclaw_1945.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Cathedral_of_Wroclaw_1945.jpg/330px-Cathedral_of_Wroclaw_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Cathedral_of_Wroclaw_1945.jpg/440px-Cathedral_of_Wroclaw_1945.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_of_Wroclaw_1945.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Wartime destruction around the cathedral, 1945
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the
       <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">
        invasion of Poland
       </a>
       , which started
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       , in September 1939, the Germans carried out mass arrests of local Polish activists and banned Polish organizations,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mc_74-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mc-74">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the city was made the headquarters of the southern district of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Selbstschutz" title="Selbstschutz">
         Selbstschutz
        </a>
       </i>
       , whose task was to persecute
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_crimes_against_the_Polish_nation" title="Nazi crimes against the Polish nation">
        Poles
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For most of the war, the fighting did not affect the city. During the war, the Germans opened the graves of medieval Polish monarchs and local dukes to carry out
       <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">
        anthropological
       </a>
       research for
       <a href="/wiki/Propaganda_in_Nazi_Germany" title="Propaganda in Nazi Germany">
        propaganda
       </a>
       purposes, wanting to demonstrate German "
       <a href="/wiki/Racial_policy_of_Nazi_Germany" title="Racial policy of Nazi Germany">
        racial purity
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gosc_39-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-gosc-39">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The remains were transported to other places by the Germans, and they have not been found to this day.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gosc_39-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-gosc-39">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1941 the remnants of the pre-war Polish minority in the city, as well as Polish slave labourers, organised a resistance group called
       <a href="/wiki/Olimp_(organization)" title="Olimp (organization)">
        Olimp
       </a>
       . The organisation gathered intelligence, carrying out sabotage and organising aid for Polish slave workers. In September 1941 the city's 10,000 Jews were expelled from their homes and soon deported to concentration camps. Few survived the
       <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">
        Holocaust
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As the war continued, refugees from bombed-out German cities, and later refugees from farther east, swelled the population to nearly one million,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wroclaw_79-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-wroclaw-79">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       including 51,000 forced labourers in 1944, and 9,876 Allied PoWs. At the end of 1944 an additional 30,000–60,000 Poles were moved into the city after the Germans crushed the
       <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising" title="Warsaw Uprising">
        Warsaw Uprising
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mikrokosmos5_80-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mikrokosmos5-80">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the war the Germans operated four
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_subcamps_of_Gross-Rosen" title="List of subcamps of Gross-Rosen">
        subcamps
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Gross-Rosen_concentration_camp" title="Gross-Rosen concentration camp">
        Gross-Rosen concentration camp
       </a>
       in the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr_81-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr-81">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Approximately 3,400-3,800 men were imprisoned in three subcamps, among them
       <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">
        Poles
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">
        Russians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">
        Italians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">
        Frenchmen
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">
        Ukrainians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">
        Czechs
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Belgians" title="Belgians">
        Belgians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavs" title="Yugoslavs">
        Yugoslavs
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">
        Chinese
       </a>
       , and about 1,500
       <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">
        Jewish
       </a>
       women were imprisoned in the fourth camp.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr_81-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr-81">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many prisoners died, and the remaining were evacuated to the main camp of Groß-Rosen in January 1945.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr_81-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr-81">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There were also three subcamps of the
       <a href="/wiki/Stalag_VIII-B" title="Stalag VIII-B">
        Stalag VIII-B/344
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Prisoner-of-war_camp" title="Prisoner-of-war camp">
        prisoner-of-war camp
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and two Nazi prisons in the city, including a youth prison, with multiple forced labour subcamps.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In February 1945 the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">
        Army
       </a>
       approached the city.
       <a href="/wiki/Gauleiter" title="Gauleiter">
        Gauleiter
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Karl_Hanke" title="Karl Hanke">
        Karl Hanke
       </a>
       declared the city a
       <i>
        Festung
       </i>
       (fortress) to be held at all costs. Hanke finally lifted a ban on the evacuation of women and children when it was almost too late. During his poorly organised evacuation in January 1945, 18,000 people froze to death in icy snowstorms of −20 °C (−4 °F) weather. By the end of the
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Breslau" title="Siege of Breslau">
        Battle of Breslau
       </a>
       (February–May 1945), half the city had been destroyed. An estimated 40,000 civilians lay dead in the ruins of homes and factories. After a siege of nearly three months, Festung Breslau capitulated to the
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">
        Red Army
       </a>
       on 6 May 1945, two days before the end of the war.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Festung_Breslau_(Breslau_Fortress)_siege_by_the_Soviet_Army_–_photo_gallery_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Festung_Breslau_(Breslau_Fortress)_siege_by_the_Soviet_Army_–_photo_gallery-85">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In August the Soviets placed the city under the control of German
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communists" title="Communists">
        communists
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mazower,_M_2008_P544_86-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mazower,_M_2008_P544-86">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Following the
       <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">
        Yalta Conference
       </a>
       held in February 1945 where the new
       <a href="/wiki/Geopolitics" title="Geopolitics">
        geopolitics
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">
        Central Europe
       </a>
       were decided, the terms of the
       <a href="/wiki/Potsdam_Conference" title="Potsdam Conference">
        Potsdam Conference
       </a>
       decreed that with almost all of Lower Silesia, the city would become part of Poland in exchange for Poland's loss of the city of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lw%C3%B3w" title="Lwów">
        Lwów
       </a>
       along with the massive territory of
       <a href="/wiki/Kresy" title="Kresy">
        Kresy
       </a>
       in the east, which was annexed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet Union
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_87-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-87">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Polish name of "Wrocław" was declared official. There had been discussion among the
       <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">
        Western Allies
       </a>
       to place the southern Polish-German boundary on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glatzer_Neisse" title="Glatzer Neisse">
        Glatzer Neisse
       </a>
       , which meant post-war Germany would have been allowed to retain approximately half of Silesia, including Breslau. However,
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">
        Stalin
       </a>
       insisted the border be drawn at the
       <a href="/wiki/Lusatian_Neisse" title="Lusatian Neisse">
        Lusatian Neisse
       </a>
       farther west.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_87-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-87">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="1945-present">
        1945-present
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1945-present">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WrocLovek_(WrocLover)_Wroclaw_dwarf_01.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5184" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/WrocLovek_%28WrocLover%29_Wroclaw_dwarf_01.JPG/170px-WrocLovek_%28WrocLover%29_Wroclaw_dwarf_01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/WrocLovek_%28WrocLover%29_Wroclaw_dwarf_01.JPG/255px-WrocLovek_%28WrocLover%29_Wroclaw_dwarf_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/WrocLovek_%28WrocLover%29_Wroclaw_dwarf_01.JPG/340px-WrocLovek_%28WrocLover%29_Wroclaw_dwarf_01.JPG 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WrocLovek_(WrocLover)_Wroclaw_dwarf_01.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw%27s_dwarfs" title="Wrocław's dwarfs">
          Wrocław dwarf
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Following
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       , the region became part of Poland under territorial changes defined by the
       <a href="/wiki/Potsdam_Agreement" title="Potsdam Agreement">
        Potsdam Agreement
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mazower,_M_2008_P544_86-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mazower,_M_2008_P544-86">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The town's inhabitants who had not fled, or who had safely returned to their home town after the war officially had ended,
       <a href="/wiki/Flight_and_expulsion_of_Germans_from_Poland_during_and_after_World_War_II" title="Flight and expulsion of Germans from Poland during and after World War II">
        were expelled
       </a>
       between 1945 and 1949 in accordance to the Potsdam Agreement and were settled in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_zone" title="Soviet occupation zone">
        Soviet occupation zone
       </a>
       or in the
       <a href="/wiki/Allied-occupied_Germany" title="Allied-occupied Germany">
        Allied Occupation Zones
       </a>
       in the remainder of Germany. The city's last pre-war German school was closed in 1963.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Polish population was dramatically increased by the resettlement of Poles during postwar
       <a href="/wiki/Polish_population_transfers_(1944%E2%80%931946)" title="Polish population transfers (1944–1946)">
        population transfers
       </a>
       during the forced
       <a href="/wiki/Deportation" title="Deportation">
        deportations
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_Poland_annexed_by_the_Soviet_Union" title="Territories of Poland annexed by the Soviet Union">
        Polish lands annexed by the Soviet Union
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Kresy" title="Kresy">
        the east
       </a>
       region, some of whom came from
       <a href="/wiki/Lviv" title="Lviv">
        Lviv
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Lwów
       </i>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Volhynia" title="Volhynia">
        Volhynia
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Vilnius_Region" title="Vilnius Region">
        Vilnius Region
       </a>
       . A small German minority (about 1,000 people, or 2% of the population) remains in the city, so that today the relation of Polish to German population is the reverse of what it was a 100 years ago.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ntkswroclaw_89-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ntkswroclaw-89">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Traces of the German past, such as inscriptions and signs, have been removed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Wrocław is now a unique European city of mixed heritage, with architecture influenced by
       <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">
        Bohemian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">
        Austrian
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">
        Prussian
       </a>
       traditions, such as Silesian
       <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">
        Gothic
       </a>
       and its
       <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">
        Baroque
       </a>
       style of court builders of Habsburg Austria (
       <a href="/wiki/Johann_Bernhard_Fischer_von_Erlach" title="Johann Bernhard Fischer von Erlach">
        Fischer von Erlach
       </a>
       ). Wrocław has a number of notable buildings by German
       <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">
        modernist
       </a>
       architects including the famous
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hala_Stulecia_(Wroc%C5%82aw)" title="Hala Stulecia (Wrocław)">
        Centennial Hall
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Hala Stulecia
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Jahrhunderthalle
       </i>
       ; 1911–1913) designed by
       <a href="/wiki/Max_Berg" title="Max Berg">
        Max Berg
       </a>
       . In 1948, Wrocław organized the
       <a href="/wiki/Recovered_Territories" title="Recovered Territories">
        Recovered Territories
       </a>
       Exhibition and the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Congress_of_Intellectuals_in_Defense_of_Peace" title="World Congress of Intellectuals in Defense of Peace">
        World Congress of Intellectuals in Defense of Peace
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Picasso" title="Picasso">
        Picasso
       </a>
       's lithograph,
       <i>
        La Colombe
       </i>
       (The Dove), a traditional, realistic picture of a pigeon, without an olive branch, was created on a napkin at the
       <a href="/wiki/Monopol_Hotel" title="Monopol Hotel">
        Monopol Hotel
       </a>
       in Wrocław during the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Congress_of_Intellectuals_in_Defense_of_Peace" title="World Congress of Intellectuals in Defense of Peace">
        World Congress of Intellectuals in Defense of Peace
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dewiza-SW.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1003" data-file-width="686" decoding="async" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Dewiza-SW.jpg/170px-Dewiza-SW.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Dewiza-SW.jpg/255px-Dewiza-SW.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Dewiza-SW.jpg/340px-Dewiza-SW.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dewiza-SW.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Fighting_Solidarity" title="Fighting Solidarity">
          Fighting Solidarity
         </a>
         logo
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1963, Wrocław was declared a
       <a href="/wiki/Closed_city" title="Closed city">
        closed city
       </a>
       because of a
       <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">
        smallpox
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Epidemic" title="Epidemic">
        epidemic
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1982, during
       <a href="/wiki/Martial_law_in_Poland" title="Martial law in Poland">
        martial law in Poland
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Anti-communism" title="Anti-communism">
        anti-communist
       </a>
       underground organizations
       <a href="/wiki/Fighting_Solidarity" title="Fighting Solidarity">
        Fighting Solidarity
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Orange_Alternative" title="Orange Alternative">
        Orange Alternative
       </a>
       were founded in Wrocław.
       <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw%27s_dwarfs" title="Wrocław's dwarfs">
        Wrocław's dwarves
       </a>
       , made of bronze, famously grew out of and commemorate Orange Alternative.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1983 and 1997,
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">
        Pope John Paul II
       </a>
       visited the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       PTV Echo, the first non-state television station in Poland and in the post-communist countries, began to broadcast in Wrocław on 6 February 1990.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In May 1997, Wrocław hosted the 46th International
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eucharistic_Congress" title="Eucharistic Congress">
        Eucharistic Congress
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In July 1997, the city was heavily affected by a
       <a href="/wiki/1997_Central_European_flood" title="1997 Central European flood">
        flood of the River Oder
       </a>
       , the worst flooding in post-war Poland, Germany, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">
        Czech Republic
       </a>
       . About one-third of the area of the city was flooded.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1997_great_flood_of_Oder_River_–_photo_gallery_97-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-1997_great_flood_of_Oder_River_–_photo_gallery-97">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The smaller
       <a href="/wiki/Widawa" title="Widawa">
        Widawa River
       </a>
       also flooded the city simultaneously, worsening the damage. An earlier, equally devastating flood of the Oder river had taken place in 1903.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1903_great_flood_of_the_Oder_river_–_photo_gallery_98-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-1903_great_flood_of_the_Oder_river_–_photo_gallery-98">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A small part of the city was also flooded during the
       <a href="/wiki/2010_Central_European_floods" title="2010 Central European floods">
        flood of 2010
       </a>
       . From 2012 to 2015, the
       <a class="extiw" href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wroc%C5%82awski_w%C4%99ze%C5%82_wodny" title="pl:Wrocławski węzeł wodny">
        Wrocław water node
       </a>
       was renovated and redeveloped to prevent further flooding.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipal_Stadium_(Wroc%C5%82aw)" title="Municipal Stadium (Wrocław)">
        Municipal Stadium
       </a>
       in Wrocław, opened in 2011, hosted three matches in Group A of the
       <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">
        UEFA Euro 2012
       </a>
       championship.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2016, Wrocław was declared the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">
        European Capital of Culture
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2017, Wrocław hosted the
       <a href="/wiki/2017_World_Games" title="2017 World Games">
        2017 World Games
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Wrocław won the
       <i>
        European Best Destination
       </i>
       title in 2018.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Wrocław is located in the three
       <a href="/wiki/Mesoregion_(geomorphology)" title="Mesoregion (geomorphology)">
        mesoregions
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Silesian_Lowlands" title="Silesian Lowlands">
        Silesian Lowlands
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw_Plain" title="Wrocław Plain">
        Wrocław Plain
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw_Valley" title="Wrocław Valley">
        Wrocław Valley
       </a>
       , Oleśnica Plain) at an elevation of around 156–170 meters (Gajowe Hill and Maślickie Hill) above sea level.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city lies on the
       <a href="/wiki/Oder" title="Oder">
        Oder
       </a>
       River and its four tributaries, which supply it within the city limits –
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bystrzyca_(Odra)" title="Bystrzyca (Odra)">
        Bystrzyca
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/O%C5%82awa_(river)" title="Oława (river)">
        Oława
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Al%C4%99za" title="Ślęza">
        Ślęza
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Widawa" title="Widawa">
        Widawa
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition, the Dobra River and many streams flow through the city. The city has a
       <a href="/wiki/Sewage_treatment" title="Sewage treatment">
        sewage treatment
       </a>
       plant on the Janówek estate.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">
        Flora and fauna
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PL-Breslau-Holzkirche-1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2487" data-file-width="2533" decoding="async" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/PL-Breslau-Holzkirche-1.jpg/220px-PL-Breslau-Holzkirche-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/PL-Breslau-Holzkirche-1.jpg/330px-PL-Breslau-Holzkirche-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/PL-Breslau-Holzkirche-1.jpg/440px-PL-Breslau-Holzkirche-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PL-Breslau-Holzkirche-1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         John of Nepomuk Church in
         <a href="/wiki/Szczytnicki_Park" title="Szczytnicki Park">
          Szczytnicki Park
         </a>
         , 16th-century
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       There are 44 city parks and public green spaces covering around 800 hectares. The most notable are
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Szczytnicki_Park" title="Szczytnicki Park">
         Szczytnicki Park
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Park Południowy
       </i>
       (South Park) and
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wladyslaw_Anders" title="Wladyslaw Anders">
         Anders
        </a>
        Park
       </i>
       . In addition, Wrocław University runs an historical
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wroc%C5%82aw_Botanical_Garden" title="University of Wrocław Botanical Garden">
        Botanical garden
       </a>
       (founded in 1811), with a salient Alpine garden, a lake and a valley.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In Wrocław, the presence of over 200 species of birds has been registered, of which over 100 have nesting places there.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As in other large Polish cities, the most numerous are
       <a href="/wiki/Rock_dove" title="Rock dove">
        pigeons
       </a>
       . Other common species are the
       <a href="/wiki/House_sparrow" title="House sparrow">
        sparrow
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_tree_sparrow" title="Eurasian tree sparrow">
        tree sparrow
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_siskin" title="Eurasian siskin">
        siskin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rook_(bird)" title="Rook (bird)">
        rook
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hooded_crow" title="Hooded crow">
        crow
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Western_jackdaw" title="Western jackdaw">
        jackdaw
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_magpie" title="Eurasian magpie">
        magpie
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Common_swift" title="Common swift">
        swift
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Common_house_martin" title="Common house martin">
        martin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Barn_swallow" title="Barn swallow">
        swallow
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Common_kestrel" title="Common kestrel">
        kestrel
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mute_swan" title="Mute swan">
        mute swan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mallard" title="Mallard">
        mallard
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_coot" title="Eurasian coot">
        coot
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Common_merganser" title="Common merganser">
        merganser
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Black-headed_gull" title="Black-headed gull">
        black-headed gull
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Great_tit" title="Great tit">
        great tit
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_blue_tit" title="Eurasian blue tit">
        blue tit
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Long-tailed_tit" title="Long-tailed tit">
        long-tailed tit
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/European_greenfinch" title="European greenfinch">
        greenfinch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hawfinch" title="Hawfinch">
        hawfinch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_collared_dove" title="Eurasian collared dove">
        collared dove
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Common_wood_pigeon" title="Common wood pigeon">
        common wood pigeon
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fieldfare" title="Fieldfare">
        fieldfare
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Redwing" title="Redwing">
        redwing
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Common_starling" title="Common starling">
        common starling
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Grey_heron" title="Grey heron">
        grey heron
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/White_stork" title="White stork">
        white stork
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Common_chaffinch" title="Common chaffinch">
        common chaffinch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Common_blackbird" title="Common blackbird">
        blackbird
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_jay" title="Eurasian jay">
        jay
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_nuthatch" title="Eurasian nuthatch">
        nuthatch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_bullfinch" title="Eurasian bullfinch">
        bullfinch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Common_cuckoo" title="Common cuckoo">
        cuckoo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_waxwing" title="Bohemian waxwing">
        waxwing
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lesser_spotted_woodpecker" title="Lesser spotted woodpecker">
        lesser spotted woodpecker
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Great_spotted_woodpecker" title="Great spotted woodpecker">
        great spotted woodpecker
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/White-backed_woodpecker" title="White-backed woodpecker">
        white-backed woodpecker
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/White_wagtail" title="White wagtail">
        white wagtail
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_blackcap" title="Eurasian blackcap">
        blackcap
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Black_redstart" title="Black redstart">
        black redstart
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_world_flycatcher" title="Old world flycatcher">
        old world flycatcher
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emberizidae" title="Emberizidae">
        emberizidae
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/European_goldfinch" title="European goldfinch">
        goldfinch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Western_marsh_harrier" title="Western marsh harrier">
        western marsh harrier
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Little_bittern" title="Little bittern">
        little bittern
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Common_moorhen" title="Common moorhen">
        common moorhen
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Common_reed_bunting" title="Common reed bunting">
        reed bunting
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Remiz" title="Remiz">
        remiz
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Great_reed_warbler" title="Great reed warbler">
        great reed warbler
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Little_crake" title="Little crake">
        little crake
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Little_ringed_plover" title="Little ringed plover">
        little ringed plover
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_eagle" title="White-tailed eagle">
        white-tailed eagle
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_109-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-auto-109">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jesienny_Park_Poludniowy.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3110" data-file-width="4628" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Jesienny_Park_Poludniowy.jpg/220px-Jesienny_Park_Poludniowy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Jesienny_Park_Poludniowy.jpg/330px-Jesienny_Park_Poludniowy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Jesienny_Park_Poludniowy.jpg/440px-Jesienny_Park_Poludniowy.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jesienny_Park_Poludniowy.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Wrocław South Park –
         <i>
          Park Południowy
         </i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In addition, the city is periodically plagued by the
       <a href="/wiki/Brown_rat" title="Brown rat">
        brown rat
       </a>
       , especially in the Market Square and in the vicinity of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eatery" title="Eatery">
        eateries
       </a>
       . Otherwise, due to the proximity of wooded areas, there are
       <a href="/wiki/Erinaceidae" title="Erinaceidae">
        hedgehogs
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Red_fox" title="Red fox">
        foxes
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">
        wild boar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bat" title="Bat">
        bats
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Beech_marten" title="Beech marten">
        martens
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Red_squirrel" title="Red squirrel">
        squirrels
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Roe_deer" title="Roe deer">
        deer
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Leporidae" title="Leporidae">
        hares
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_beaver" title="Eurasian beaver">
        beavers
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/European_polecat" title="European polecat">
        polecats
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_otter" title="Eurasian otter">
        otters
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/European_badger" title="European badger">
        badgers
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Least_weasel" title="Least weasel">
        weasels
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Stoat" title="Stoat">
        stoats
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raccoon_dog" title="Raccoon dog">
        raccoon dogs
       </a>
       . There are also occasional sightings of escaped
       <a href="/wiki/Muskrat" title="Muskrat">
        muskrat
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/American_mink" title="American mink">
        american mink
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Raccoon" title="Raccoon">
        raccoon
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_109-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-auto-109">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Air_pollution">
        Air pollution
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Air pollution">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mapa-zanieczyszczena.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="572" data-file-width="638" decoding="async" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Mapa-zanieczyszczena.jpg/220px-Mapa-zanieczyszczena.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Mapa-zanieczyszczena.jpg/330px-Mapa-zanieczyszczena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Mapa-zanieczyszczena.jpg/440px-Mapa-zanieczyszczena.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mapa-zanieczyszczena.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of Wrocław's areas where PM10 standards were exceeded in 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Air pollution is a considerable issue in Wrocław. In a report by French
       <i>
        Respire
       </i>
       organization, from 2014, Wrocław was ranked the eighth most polluted European city, with 166 days of bad air quality per year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TVN_smog_111-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-TVN_smog-111">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Heavy air pollution mainly occurs in the colder months, during
       <a href="/wiki/Autumn" title="Autumn">
        autumn
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Winter" title="Winter">
        winter
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw_University" title="Wrocław University">
        Wrocław University
       </a>
       research from 2017, high concentration of
       <a href="/wiki/Particulates" title="Particulates">
        particular matters (PM2.5 and PM 10)
       </a>
       in the air causes 942 premature deaths of Wrocław inhabitants per year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Uniwersytet_113-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Uniwersytet-113">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Air pollution also causes 3297 cases of bronchitis among Wrocław's children per year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Uniwersytet_113-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Uniwersytet-113">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Approximately 84% of residents believe that air pollution is a serious social problem, according to a poll from May 2017, and 73% of people believe that air quality is poor.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
        <a href="#cite_note-114">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2012, there were 71 days, when the PM10 standards, set by
       <a href="/wiki/Air_quality_and_EU_legislation" title="Air quality and EU legislation">
        Cleaner Air For Europe Directive
       </a>
       , were exceeded. In 2014, there were 104 such days.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
        <a href="#cite_note-115">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2014, the inhabitants founded an organization called the
       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Silesian_Voivodeship" title="Lower Silesian Voivodeship">
        Lower Silesian
       </a>
       Smog Alert (
       <i>
        Dolnośląski Alarm Smogowy, DAS
       </i>
       ), to address the air pollution problem. Its goals are to educate the public and to reduce emission of harmful substances.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
        <a href="#cite_note-116">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       According to Köppen's original definition, Wrocław has an
       <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">
        oceanic climate
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Köppen climate classification
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        Cfb
       </i>
       ). However it is common in the literature published in English to use the 0 °C isotherm for the coldest month (as opposed to the original −3 °C) as the boundary between the
       <i>
        C
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        D
       </i>
       types.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2021)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Based on that definition, Wrocław has a
       <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">
        humid continental climate
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Dfb
       </i>
       ). It is one of the warmest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Poland" title="List of cities in Poland">
        cities in Poland
       </a>
       . Lying in the
       <a href="/wiki/Silesian_Lowlands" title="Silesian Lowlands">
        Silesian Lowlands
       </a>
       between
       <a href="/wiki/Trzebnickie_Hills" title="Trzebnickie Hills">
        Trzebnickie Hills
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Sudetes" title="Sudetes">
        Sudetes
       </a>
       , the mean annual temperature is 9.04 °C (48 °F). The coldest month is January (average temperature −0.7 °C), with snow being common in winter, and the warmest is July (average temperature 18.9 °C). The highest temperature in Wrocław was recorded on 19 August 1892
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and 8 August 2015 (+38.9 °C).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
        <a href="#cite_note-118">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The previous records were +38 °C on 27 June 1935 and +37.9 °C on 31 July 1994. The lowest temperature was recorded on 11 February 1956 (−32 °C).
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">
        Government and politics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Government and politics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nowy_Ratusz_(01).JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Nowy_Ratusz_%2801%29.JPG/220px-Nowy_Ratusz_%2801%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Nowy_Ratusz_%2801%29.JPG/330px-Nowy_Ratusz_%2801%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Nowy_Ratusz_%2801%29.JPG/440px-Nowy_Ratusz_%2801%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nowy_Ratusz_(01).JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Wrocław New City Hall – the seat of the city mayor
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="List of mayors of Wrocław">
        List of mayors of Wrocław
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Wrocław is the capital city of
       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Silesian_Voivodeship" title="Lower Silesian Voivodeship">
        Lower Silesian Voivodeship
       </a>
       , a province (
       <a href="/wiki/Voivodeships_of_Poland" title="Voivodeships of Poland">
        voivodeship
       </a>
       ) created in 1999. It was previously the seat of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw_Voivodeship" title="Wrocław Voivodeship">
        Wrocław Voivodeship
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
        <a href="#cite_note-125">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city is a separate urban
       <a href="/wiki/Gmina" title="Gmina">
        gmina
       </a>
       and city-county (
       <a href="/wiki/Powiat" title="Powiat">
        powiat
       </a>
       ). It is also the seat of
       <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw_County" title="Wrocław County">
        Wrocław County
       </a>
       , which adjoins but does not include the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
        <a href="#cite_note-126">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Districts">
        Districts
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Districts">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Districts of Wrocław">
        Districts of Wrocław
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wroclaw_city_districts.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2011" data-file-width="2698" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Wroclaw_city_districts.png/220px-Wroclaw_city_districts.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Wroclaw_city_districts.png/330px-Wroclaw_city_districts.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Wroclaw_city_districts.png/440px-Wroclaw_city_districts.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wroclaw_city_districts.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Wrocław boroughs (until 1990)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Osiedla_wroclaw.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6623" data-file-width="9362" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Osiedla_wroclaw.png/220px-Osiedla_wroclaw.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Osiedla_wroclaw.png/330px-Osiedla_wroclaw.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Osiedla_wroclaw.png/440px-Osiedla_wroclaw.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Osiedla_wroclaw.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The 48 administrative district quarters (since 1990)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Wrocław was previously subdivided into five boroughs (
       <a href="/wiki/Dzielnica" title="Dzielnica">
        dzielnica
       </a>
       ):
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw-Fabryczna" title="Wrocław-Fabryczna">
         Fabryczna
        </a>
        ("Factory Quarter")
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
         <a href="#cite_note-127">
          [126]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Krzyki" title="Krzyki">
         Krzyki
        </a>
        , (
        <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
         German
        </a>
        :
        <i lang="de">
         Krietern
        </i>
        , meaning "Wranglers")
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStawaszMarszał200641_128-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStawaszMarszał200641-128">
          [127]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Psie_Pole" title="Psie Pole">
         Psie Pole
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
         German
        </a>
        :
        <i lang="de">
         Hundsfeld
        </i>
        , "Dogs' Field", named after the alleged
        <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hundsfeld" title="Battle of Hundsfeld">
         Battle of Psie Pole
        </a>
        )
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStawaszMarszał200641_128-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStawaszMarszał200641-128">
          [127]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw-Stare_Miasto" title="Wrocław-Stare Miasto">
         Stare Miasto
        </a>
        (old town)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStawaszMarszał200641_128-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStawaszMarszał200641-128">
          [127]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw-%C5%9Ar%C3%B3dmie%C5%9Bcie" title="Wrocław-Śródmieście">
         Śródmieście
        </a>
        (midtown)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStawaszMarszał200641_128-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStawaszMarszał200641-128">
          [127]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Since 1990, the city has been divided into 48 district quarters (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Osiedle" title="Osiedle">
         osiedle
        </a>
       </i>
       ) – Bieńkowice, Biskupin-Sępolno-Dąbie-Bartoszowice, Borek, Brochów, Gaj, Gajowice, Gądów-Popowice Płd., Grabiszyn-Grabiszynek, Huby, Jagodno, Jerzmanowo-Jarnołtów-Strachowice-Osiniec, Karłowice-Różanka, Klecina, Kleczków, Kowale, Krzyki-Partynice, Księże, Kuźniki, Leśnica, Lipa Piotrowska, Maślice, Muchobór Mały, Muchobór Wielki,
       <a href="/wiki/Nadodrze" title="Nadodrze">
        Nadodrze
       </a>
       , Nowy Dwór, Ołbin, Ołtaszyn, Oporów, Osobowice-Rędzin, Pawłowice, Pilczyce-Kozanów-Popowice Płn.,
       <a href="/wiki/Plac_Grunwaldzki_(osiedle)" title="Plac Grunwaldzki (osiedle)">
        Plac Grunwaldzki
       </a>
       , Polanowice-Poświętne-Ligota, Powstańców Śląskich, Pracze Odrzańskie, Przedmieście Oławskie, Przedmieście Świdnickie, Psie Pole-Zawidawie, Sołtysowice, Stare Miasto, Strachocin-Swojczyce-Wojnów, Szczepin, Świniary, Tarnogaj, Widawa, Wojszyce, Zacisze-Zalesie-Szczytniki, and Żerniki.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
        <a href="#cite_note-129">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_government">
        Municipal government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Municipal government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Wrocław is currently governed by the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Wroc%C5%82aw" title="List of mayors of Wrocław">
        city's mayor
       </a>
       and a municipal legislature known as the city council. The city council is made up of 39 councilors and is directly elected by the city's inhabitants. The remit of the council and president extends to all areas of municipal policy and development planning, up to and including development of local infrastructure, transport and planning permission. However, it is not able to draw taxation directly from its citizens, and instead receives its budget from the Polish national government whose seat is in Warsaw.
      </p>
      <p>
       The city's current mayor is
       <a href="/wiki/Jacek_Sutryk" title="Jacek Sutryk">
        Jacek Sutryk
       </a>
       , who has served in this position since 2018. The first mayor of Wrocław after the war was
       <a href="/wiki/Boles%C5%82aw_Drobner" title="Bolesław Drobner">
        Bolesław Drobner
       </a>
       , appointed to the position on March 14, 1945, before the surrender of Festung Breslau.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wroc%C5%82aw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Poland" title="Economy of Poland">
        Economy of Poland
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2017_Sky_Tower_we_Wroc%C5%82awiu.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3482" data-file-width="2234" decoding="async" height="281" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/2017_Sky_Tower_we_Wroc%C5%82awiu.jpg/180px-2017_Sky_Tower_we_Wroc%C5%82awiu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/2017_Sky_Tower_we_Wroc%C5%82awiu.jpg/270px-2017_Sky_Tower_we_Wroc%C5%82awiu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/2017_Sky_Tower_we_Wroc%C5%82awiu.jpg/360px-2017_Sky_Tower_we_Wroc%C5%82awiu.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2017_Sky_Tower_we_Wroc%C5%82awiu.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Sky_Tower_(Wroc%C5%82aw)" title="Sky Tower (Wrocław)">
          Sky Tower
         </a>
         is one of the
         <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Poland" title="List of tallest buildings in Poland">
          tallest buildings in Poland
         </a>
         . It offers office, commercial, residential and recreational space.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Wrocław is the second-wealthiest of the large cities in Poland after
       <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">
        Warsaw
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
        <a href="#cite_note-130">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city is also home to the largest number of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leasing" title="Leasing">
        leasing
       </a>
       and debt collection companies in the country, including the largest European Leasing Fund as well as numerous banks. Due to the proximity of the borders with Germany and the Czech Republic, Wrocław and the region of
       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Silesia" title="Lower Silesia">
        Lower Silesia
       </a>
       is a large import and export partner with these countries.
      </p>
      <p>
       Wrocław's industry manufactures
       <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">
        buses
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Railroad_car" title="Railroad car">
        railroad cars
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Home_appliance" title="Home appliance">
        home appliances
       </a>
       , chemicals, and electronics. The city houses factories and development centers of many foreign and domestic corporations, such as
       <a href="/wiki/WAGO_Kontakttechnik" title="WAGO Kontakttechnik">
        WAGO Kontakttechnik
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">
        Siemens
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bosch_GmbH" title="Robert Bosch GmbH">
        Bosch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Whirlpool_Corporation" title="Whirlpool Corporation">
        Whirlpool Corporation
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nokia_Networks" title="Nokia Networks">
        Nokia Networks
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Volvo" title="Volvo">
        Volvo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">
        HP
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">
        IBM
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">
        Google
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opera_Software" title="Opera Software">
        Opera Software
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Transportation" title="Bombardier Transportation">
        Bombardier Transportation
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/WABCO_Vehicle_Control_Systems" title="WABCO Vehicle Control Systems">
        WABCO
       </a>
       and others. Wrocław is also the location of offices for large Polish companies including
       <a href="/wiki/Getin_Holding" title="Getin Holding">
        Getin Holding
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/AmRest" title="AmRest">
        AmRest
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Polmos" title="Polmos">
        Polmos
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MCI_Management_SA" title="MCI Management SA">
        MCI Management SA
       </a>
       . Additionally,
       <a href="/wiki/Kaufland" title="Kaufland">
        Kaufland
       </a>
       Poland has its main headquarters in the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
        <a href="#cite_note-131">
         [130]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since the beginning of the 21st century, the city has had a developing
       <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">
        high-tech
       </a>
       sector.
Many high-tech companies are located in the Wrocław Technology Park, such as Baluff, CIT Engineering, Caisson Elektronik, ContiTech, Ericsson, Innovative Software Technologies,
       <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">
        IBM
       </a>
       , IT-MED, IT Sector,
       <a href="/wiki/Livechat_Software" title="Livechat Software">
        LiveChat Software
       </a>
       , Mitsubishi Electric, Maas, PGS Software, Technology Transfer Agency Techtra and Vratis. In
       <a href="/wiki/Biskupice_Podg%C3%B3rne" title="Biskupice Podgórne">
        Biskupice Podgórne
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Gmina_Kobierzyce" title="Gmina Kobierzyce">
        Community Kobierzyce
       </a>
       ) there are factories of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LG" title="LG">
        LG
       </a>
       (LG Display, LG Electronics, LG Chem, LG Innotek), Dong Seo Display, Dong Yang Electronics,
       <a href="/wiki/Toshiba" title="Toshiba">
        Toshiba
       </a>
       , and many other companies, mainly from the electronics and home appliances sectors, while the
       <a href="/wiki/Nowa_Wie%C5%9B_Wroc%C5%82awska" title="Nowa Wieś Wrocławska">
        Nowa Wieś Wrocławska
       </a>
       factory and distribution center of
       <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9" title="Nestlé">
        Nestlé
       </a>
       Purina and factories a few other enterprises.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DH_Kameleon.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1100" data-file-width="968" decoding="async" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/DH_Kameleon.jpg/220px-DH_Kameleon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/DH_Kameleon.jpg/330px-DH_Kameleon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/DH_Kameleon.jpg/440px-DH_Kameleon.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DH_Kameleon.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Petersdorff Department Store designed by
         <a href="/wiki/Erich_Mendelsohn" title="Erich Mendelsohn">
          Erich Mendelsohn
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The city is the seat of Wrocław Research Centre
       <a href="/wiki/European_Institute_of_Innovation_and_Technology" title="European Institute of Innovation and Technology">
        EIT
       </a>
       +, which contains, inter alia, geological research laboratories to the unconventional and Lower Silesian Cluster of Nanotechnology.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
        <a href="#cite_note-132">
         [131]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The logistics centers
       <a href="/wiki/DHL" title="DHL">
        DHL
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/FedEx" title="FedEx">
        FedEx
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/United_Parcel_Service" title="United Parcel Service">
        UPS
       </a>
       are based in Wrocław.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
        <a href="#cite_note-133">
         [132]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Furthermore, it is a major center for the pharmaceutical industry (U.S. Pharmacia, Hasco-Lek, Galena, Avec Pharma,
       <a href="/wiki/3M" title="3M">
        3M
       </a>
       , Labor, S-Lab, Herbapol, and Cezal).
      </p>
      <p>
       Wrocław is home to Poland's largest
       <a href="/wiki/Shopping_mall" title="Shopping mall">
        shopping mall
       </a>
       –
       <a class="extiw" href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aleja_Bielany" title="pl:Aleja Bielany">
        Bielany Avenue
       </a>
       (pl. Aleja Bielany) and Bielany Trade Center, located in
       <a href="/wiki/Bielany_Wroc%C5%82awskie" title="Bielany Wrocławskie">
        Bielany Wrocławskie
       </a>
       where stores such as
       <a href="/wiki/Auchan" title="Auchan">
        Auchan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Decathlon_(retailer)" title="Decathlon (retailer)">
        Decathlon
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Leroy_Merlin" title="Leroy Merlin">
        Leroy Merlin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Makro" title="Makro">
        Makro
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tesco" title="Tesco">
        Tesco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/IKEA" title="IKEA">
        IKEA
       </a>
       , Jula,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Obi_(store)" title="Obi (store)">
        OBI
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Castorama" title="Castorama">
        Castorama
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Black_Red_White" title="Black Red White">
        Black Red White
       </a>
       , Poco,
       <a href="/wiki/E._Wedel" title="E. Wedel">
        E. Wedel
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cargill" title="Cargill">
        Cargill
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Prologis" title="Prologis">
        Prologis
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Panattoni" title="Panattoni">
        Panattoni
       </a>
       can be found.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
        <a href="#cite_note-134">
         [133]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In February 2013,
       <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">
        Qatar Airways
       </a>
       launched its Wrocław European Customer Service.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
        <a href="#cite_note-135">
         [134]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Techland" title="Techland">
          Techland
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tieto" title="Tieto">
          Tieto
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/UBS" title="UBS">
          UBS
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/United_Parcel_Service" title="United Parcel Service">
          UPS
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Technologies_Corporation" title="United Technologies Corporation">
          United Technologies Corporation
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Viessmann" title="Viessmann">
          Viessmann
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Volvo" title="Volvo">
          Volvo
         </a>
         Polska sp. z o.o.
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/WABCO_Vehicle_Control_Systems" title="WABCO Vehicle Control Systems">
          WABCO Polska
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Whirlpool_Corporation" title="Whirlpool Corporation">

         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
      </div>
